<p><b>Marco Reus</b> (<small>German pronunciation:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[mako s]</a></span>; born 31 May 1989) is a German professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays for and <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captains</a> <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> club <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany national team</a>.
</p><p>Reus spent his youth career at Borussia Dortmund, prior to leaving for <a href="/wiki/Rot_Weiss_Ahlen" title="Rot Weiss Ahlen">Rot Weiss Ahlen</a>. He joined <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a> in 2009, and had his most successful season in 2012, scoring 18 goals and providing 12 assists in the Bundesliga to help Borussia Mönchengladbach secure a place in the following season's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>. Reus returned to his hometown club Borussia Dortmund at the end of that season, helping the club reaching the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Champions League Final">2013 UEFA Champions League Final</a> in his first season. With Dortmund, Reus won three <a href="/wiki/DFL-Supercup" title="DFL-Supercup">DFL-Supercups</a> (in <a href="/wiki/2013_DFL-Supercup" title="2013 DFL-Supercup">2013</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_DFL-Supercup" title="2014 DFL-Supercup">2014</a> and <a href="/wiki/2019_DFL-Supercup" title="2019 DFL-Supercup">2019</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> in <a href="/wiki/2017_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2017 DFB-Pokal Final">2017</a>, and he has scored over 100 goals for the club. He has been named Bundesliga Player of the Season on three occasions.
</p><p>With the Germany national team, Reus has only 44 caps, due to his recurring injuries in recent years. He missed the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>, which Germany won, but played in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Reus was born in <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>, North Rhine-Westphalia.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He began to play football for his hometown club Post SV Dortmund in 1994 and joined the youth ranks of <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> He played for <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> until he left for the U-19 team of <a href="/wiki/Rot_Weiss_Ahlen" title="Rot Weiss Ahlen">Rot Weiss Ahlen</a> in the summer of 2006. During his first year there, he played as an attacking midfielder and was featured in six games for the club's second team, which played in the Westphalia league at the time. He scored a goal in each of his first two games. The following year, he was able to break into Ahlen's first team, which played in the German third division at the time. He featured in 16 games that season, two of which he started. His only goal came on the last matchday, where he played the full 90 minutes for the first time that season, and propelled the team to promotion into the <a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">2. Bundesliga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 2008–09, as a 19-year-old, he had his definitive breakthrough as a professional football player, playing 27 games and scoring four goals.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Borussia_M.C3.B6nchengladbach"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Borussia_Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Borussia Mönchengladbach">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marco_reusbmg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Marco_reusbmg.jpg/180px-Marco_reusbmg.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Marco_reusbmg.jpg/270px-Marco_reusbmg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Marco_reusbmg.jpg/360px-Marco_reusbmg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="420" data-file-height="495" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marco_reusbmg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reus with <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a> in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>On 25 May 2009, Reus signed a four-year contract with Bundesliga club <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>On 28 August 2009, he scored his first Bundesliga goal in a game against <a href="/wiki/1._FSV_Mainz_05" title="1. FSV Mainz 05">Mainz 05</a> after a 50-metre solo run,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and since then became a prolific goalscorer for his club under <a href="/wiki/Lucien_Favre" title="Lucien Favre">Lucien Favre</a>. 
</p><p>On 20 August 2010, Reus scored his first Bundesliga brace in an eventual loss against 1. FSV Mainz 05.
</p><p>On 19 November 2011, he scored his first ever Bundesliga hat-trick in a 5-0 trashing against <a href="/wiki/Werder_Bremen" class="mw-redirect" title="Werder Bremen">Werder Bremen</a>.
</p><p>At the start of the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Bundesliga" title="2011–12 Bundesliga">2011–12 season</a>, Reus began the season in fine form, scoring 10 goals in his first 13 matches. His contract with Gladbach was set to expire in 2015 and reportedly had a buy-out clause of €18&#160;million. Reus mentioned that his role model was <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Rosick%C3%BD" title="Tomáš Rosický">Tomáš Rosický</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Borussia_Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Borussia Dortmund">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="2012.E2.80.9313_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–13_season">2012–13 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2012–13 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 4 January 2012, Reus signed with his former club Borussia Dortmund for a €17.1&#160;million transfer fee on a five-year deal. He spoke about his transfer saying, "I've made the decision to take the next step forward in the coming season. I'd like to play for a club who can challenge for the league title and guarantee me Champions League football. I see this chance in Dortmund."<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Reus officially re-joined Dortmund on 1 July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
In Reus's Bundesliga debut with Dortmund on 24 August, he scored a goal as his new side completed a 2–1 win over <a href="/wiki/SV_Werder_Bremen" title="SV Werder Bremen">Werder Bremen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> On 29 September, Reus scored two goals for Dortmund in a 5–0 rout of his former club Borussia Mönchengladbach, pushing the champions to the top of the Bundesliga table through six games.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 October, in Reus's second ever <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> appearance, he opened the scoring as Dortmund earned a 1–1 draw away to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He then opened the scoring for the German champions in their 2–2 draw with <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium" title="Santiago Bernabéu Stadium">Santiago Bernabéu Stadium</a> on 6 November, netting on a spectacular <a href="/wiki/Volley_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Volley (football)">volley</a> after a kick-down from teammate <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lewandowski" title="Robert Lewandowski">Robert Lewandowski</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In Dortmund's following Champions League match, on 21 November, Reus scored Dortmund's first goal in a 4–1 defeat of <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Arena">Amsterdam Arena</a>, securing qualification for the Round of 16 as Group D winners.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 February 2013, Reus scored a hat-trick, netting all the goals in Dortmund's thumping of <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hessian</a> side <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> On 11 May, Reus scored a late brace against <a href="/wiki/VfL_Wolfsburg" title="VfL Wolfsburg">VfL Wolfsburg</a> to help Dortmund draw the match after being two goals down.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 April 2013, Reus scored an injury time goal which was a vital one in the stunning injury time comeback against <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_CF" title="Málaga CF">Malaga</a> in the quarter final leg 2 of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Dortmund won the match by 3-2 and progressed on to the next round where they defeated <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> 4–3 on aggregate to reach the final.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2013.E2.80.9314_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–14_season">2013–14 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2013–14 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marco_Reus_2013.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Marco_Reus_2013.jpeg/180px-Marco_Reus_2013.jpeg" decoding="async" width="180" height="276" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Marco_Reus_2013.jpeg/270px-Marco_Reus_2013.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Marco_Reus_2013.jpeg/360px-Marco_Reus_2013.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="439" data-file-height="672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marco_Reus_2013.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reus in action for <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>On 27 July 2013, in the <a href="/wiki/2013_DFL-Supercup" title="2013 DFL-Supercup">2013 DFL-Supercup</a> against <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>, Reus netted the game's opening goal and later rounded off the scoring, as Borussia Dortmund claimed a 4–2 victory to lift the trophy.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 August, Reus converted a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty kick</a> which rounded off the scoring as Dortmund defeated <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Braunschweig" title="Eintracht Braunschweig">Eintracht Braunschweig</a> 2–1 at the <a href="/wiki/Signal_Iduna_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Signal Iduna Park">Signal Iduna Park</a> in the second game of Dortmund's <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Bundesliga" title="2013–14 Bundesliga">2013–14</a> league campaign. He then scored a brace against <a href="/wiki/SC_Freiburg" title="SC Freiburg">SC Freiburg</a>, one from the penalty spot, and started the season hitting impressive form. Reus had confirmed he would be Dortmund's penalty taker for the season, though despite winning a penalty against <a href="/wiki/TSV_1860_Munich" title="TSV 1860 Munich">1860 Munich</a> in the DFB Pokal, he allowed teammate <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Emerick_Aubameyang" title="Pierre-Emerick Aubameyang">Pierre-Emerick Aubameyang</a> in taking the penalty which propelled the Borussia-based club into the next round of the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> On 1 November 2013, Reus scored a goal for Dortmund in a 6–1 win against <a href="/wiki/VfB_Stuttgart" title="VfB Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</a> in the Bundesliga.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 February 2014, Reus scored a goal in a 4–2 win for Dortmund against <a href="/wiki/FC_Zenit_Saint_Petersburg" title="FC Zenit Saint Petersburg">Zenit Saint Petersburg</a> in the first leg of the round of 16 in the UEFA Champions League.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> On 29 March, he then scored a hat-trick in a 3–2 win for Dortmund against VfB Stuttgart in the Bundesliga.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> On 8 April, Reus scored twice in Borussia Dortmund's second leg 2–0 win against Real Madrid, though Dortmund were eventually knocked out of the competition after losing 3–2 on aggregate.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Reus finished the season with 23 goals and 18 assists in all competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2014.E2.80.9315_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–15_season">2014–15 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2014–15 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the second match of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Bundesliga" title="2014–15 Bundesliga">2014–15 Bundesliga</a> against <a href="/wiki/FC_Augsburg" title="FC Augsburg">FC Augsburg</a>, Reus scored one goal and helped set up another. Dortmund went to win the match by 3–2.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In September 2014, he was diagnosed with an ankle injury.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> On 22 October 2014, having returned from injury,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Reus contributed a goal and assist in their 4–0 <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Champions_League#Group_D" title="2014–15 UEFA Champions League">Champions League group stage</a> away win against <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> On 1 November, he scored the only goal for Dortmund in their 2–1 away loss against their rivals Bayern Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite prior injury concerns, Reus started Dortmund's match away to <a href="/wiki/SC_Paderborn_07" title="SC Paderborn 07">SC Paderborn</a> on 22 November and scored to put them 2–0 up. He was stretchered off in the second half, however, after which Paderborn equalised for a final score of 2–2.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The injury ruled him out until January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 February 2015, Reus signed a contract extension with Dortmund, keeping him at the club until 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.9316_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–16_season">2015–16 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2015–16 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 5 August 2015, Reus scored a goal in Borussia Dortmund's 5–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Wolfsberger_AC" title="Wolfsberger AC">Wolfsberger AC</a> to advance into the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Europa_League_qualifying_phase_and_play-off_round" class="mw-redirect" title="2015–16 UEFA Europa League qualifying phase and play-off round">2015–16 Europa League play-off round</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On 15 August, he then opened the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Bundesliga" title="2015–16 Bundesliga">2015–16</a> league campaign with a goal and an assist in a 4–0 home win against his former club Borussia Mönchengladbach.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On 28 August 2015, he scored a hat-trick in their 7–2 home win against <a href="/wiki/Odds_BK" title="Odds BK">Odds BK</a> to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2015–16 UEFA Europa League">2015–16 UEFA Europa League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 April 2016, Reus was one of three goalscorers as Borussia won 3–0 away at <a href="/wiki/Hertha_BSC" title="Hertha BSC">Hertha BSC</a> in the semi-final of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_DFB-Pokal" title="2015–16 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Before the start of the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Bundesliga" title="2016–17 Bundesliga">2016–17 Bundesliga</a>, he became the captain for Borussia Dortmund shortly after former club captain <a href="/wiki/Mats_Hummels" title="Mats Hummels">Mats Hummels</a> left for rivals Bayern Munich. He finished the 2015–16 season with total of 23 goals and 8 assists in 43 appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.9317_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–17_season">2016–17 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2016–17 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After being sidelined due to injury, Reus made his return on 22 November 2016. He scored twice and assisted once in a historic 8–4 Champions league group stage win against <a href="/wiki/Legia_Warsaw" title="Legia Warsaw">Legia Warsaw</a>. Reus took the game ball for it was originally a hat-trick game by him.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> On 3 December 2016, he assisted three goals in their 4–1 win against his former club Borussia Mönchengladbach.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Four days later, Reus scored in a 2–2 draw against Real Madrid; Dortmund subsequently advanced to the round 16 as the winners of Group F, ahead of Madrid.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 10 December 2016, Reus continued his goalscoring form with a late equaliser in Dortmund's 1–1 draw with <a href="/wiki/1._FC_K%C3%B6ln" title="1. FC Köln">1. FC Köln</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/2017_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2017 DFB-Pokal Final">2017 DFB-Pokal Final</a>, Reus suffered a partial cruciate ligament tear and was substituted at halftime. Dortmund went on to win the match, giving Reus his first major trophy.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The initial prognosis suggested that he would miss "several" months.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–18_season">2017–18 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2017–18 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FC_Salzburg_gegen_Borussia_Dortmund_(EL_Achtelfinale_R%C3%BCckspiel_15._M%C3%A4rz_2018)_43.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/FC_Salzburg_gegen_Borussia_Dortmund_%28EL_Achtelfinale_R%C3%BCckspiel_15._M%C3%A4rz_2018%29_43.jpg/220px-FC_Salzburg_gegen_Borussia_Dortmund_%28EL_Achtelfinale_R%C3%BCckspiel_15._M%C3%A4rz_2018%29_43.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/FC_Salzburg_gegen_Borussia_Dortmund_%28EL_Achtelfinale_R%C3%BCckspiel_15._M%C3%A4rz_2018%29_43.jpg/330px-FC_Salzburg_gegen_Borussia_Dortmund_%28EL_Achtelfinale_R%C3%BCckspiel_15._M%C3%A4rz_2018%29_43.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/FC_Salzburg_gegen_Borussia_Dortmund_%28EL_Achtelfinale_R%C3%BCckspiel_15._M%C3%A4rz_2018%29_43.jpg/440px-FC_Salzburg_gegen_Borussia_Dortmund_%28EL_Achtelfinale_R%C3%BCckspiel_15._M%C3%A4rz_2018%29_43.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1775" data-file-height="2039" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FC_Salzburg_gegen_Borussia_Dortmund_(EL_Achtelfinale_R%C3%BCckspiel_15._M%C3%A4rz_2018)_43.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reus in 2018</div></div></div>
<p>On 10 February 2018, Reus recovered from the ligament damage and made his return against <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburg</a> in the Bundesliga.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Reus scored his first goal since his return from injury and the only goal in the match against his former club Borussia Mönchengladbach in a 1–0 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Reus scored Dortmund's only goal in two consecutive matches against Augsburg and <a href="/wiki/RB_Leipzig" title="RB Leipzig">RB Leipzig</a> in which both the matches ended in a 1–1 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On 9 March 2018, Reus extended his contract with the club until 30 June 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On 21 April, Reus scored twice in a 4–0 win over Bayer Leverkusen, where he also missed a penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> On 29 April, Reus scored a 19th-minute goal in Dortmund's 1–1 draw with Werder Bremen.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On 12 May 2018, Reus scored the only goal for the team in Dortmund's 3–1 loss to Hoffenheim.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Reus finished the season with 7 goals in 15 appearances in all competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2018.E2.80.9319_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–19_season">2018–19 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2018–19 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Prior to the start of the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Borussia_Dortmund_season" title="2018–19 Borussia Dortmund season">2018–19</a> season, Reus was made club captain by incoming coach <a href="/wiki/Lucien_Favre" title="Lucien Favre">Lucien Favre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> On 21 August 2018, Reus scored the winning goal in <a href="/wiki/Overtime_(sports)" title="Overtime (sports)">extra time</a> to help his side earn a 2–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/SpVgg_Greuther_F%C3%BCrth" title="SpVgg Greuther Fürth">SpVgg Greuther Fürth</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_DFB-Pokal" title="2018–19 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> first round match.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Reus scored a 90th-minute goal which was his 100th Bundesliga goal as Dortmund defeated RB Leipzig with a 4–1 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On 27 September, he scored two goals including his 100th goal for Borussia Dortmund across all competitions in a 7–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">1. FC Nürnberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 November 2018, he scored back to back goals in the second half of <a href="/wiki/Der_Klassiker" title="Der Klassiker">Der Klassiker</a> against Bayern Munich as Dortmund came from behind to win the match 3–2.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The game kept Dortmund on top of the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> table, 7 points ahead of Bayern Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reus ended the season with 21 goals and 14 assists in all competitions,<sup id="cite_ref-2018/19_stats_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018/19_stats-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> and was voted the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Footballer_of_the_Year_(Germany)" title="Footballer of the Year (Germany)">Germany Footballer of the year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gdansk_PGE_Arena_GER-GRE_Euro_2012_08_Reus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Gdansk_PGE_Arena_GER-GRE_Euro_2012_08_Reus.jpg/130px-Gdansk_PGE_Arena_GER-GRE_Euro_2012_08_Reus.jpg" decoding="async" width="130" height="284" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Gdansk_PGE_Arena_GER-GRE_Euro_2012_08_Reus.jpg/195px-Gdansk_PGE_Arena_GER-GRE_Euro_2012_08_Reus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Gdansk_PGE_Arena_GER-GRE_Euro_2012_08_Reus.jpg/260px-Gdansk_PGE_Arena_GER-GRE_Euro_2012_08_Reus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="318" data-file-height="694" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gdansk_PGE_Arena_GER-GRE_Euro_2012_08_Reus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reus playing for <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> in 2012</div></div></div>
<p>On 11 August 2009, Reus made his <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_under-21_football_team" title="Germany national under-21 football team">Germany under-21</a> debut in a friendly match against <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_under-21_football_team" title="Turkey national under-21 football team">Turkey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> On 6 May 2010, he earned his first call-up to the <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">senior team</a><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> for a friendly match against <a href="/wiki/Malta_national_football_team" title="Malta national football team">Malta</a> on 14 May 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On 11 May 2010, he withdrew from the squad due to a leg injury picked up in the last game of the season against <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> On 7 October 2011, he made his debut against <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_football_team" title="Turkey national football team">Turkey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for the team on 26 May 2012 in a 5–3 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On 22 June, he scored in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> quarter-final against <a href="/wiki/Greece_national_football_team" title="Greece national football team">Greece</a>, his first start for Germany in the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reus established himself as a regular member of <a href="/wiki/Joachim_L%C3%B6w" title="Joachim Löw">Joachim Löw</a>'s side in the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">2014 FIFA World Cup qualification campaign</a>, scoring five goals and registering three assists in six matches.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> He was named in Germany's squad for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">World Cup finals</a>, but was ultimately forced to withdraw after suffering an ankle injury in the team's 6–1 warm-up win against <a href="/wiki/Armenia_national_football_team" title="Armenia national football team">Armenia</a> on 6 June.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reus made his international comeback in Germany's first post-World Cup friendly against <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> on 3 September 2014. However, the world champions were defeated 4–2 by the side they had beaten in the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2014 FIFA World Cup Final">World Cup final</a> two months earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">qualification</a> for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>, Reus made four appearances, scoring once in a 2–0 defeat of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_national_football_team" title="Georgia national football team">Georgia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a> but was not selected for the tournament after suffering a groin injury.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 June 2018, Reus made his return to international duty after two years in a friendly match against <a href="/wiki/Austria_national_football_team" title="Austria national football team">Austria</a>, which ended in a 2–1 loss for Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Reus was included in Joachim Löw's 23-man final squad for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> on 4 June 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> On 17 June, Reus made his first <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> appearance during their opening match against <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> as a substitute by replacing <a href="/wiki/Sami_Khedira" title="Sami Khedira">Sami Khedira</a> in the 60th minute, but the match ended in a 1–0 loss for Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On 23 June, Reus scored an equalizing goal and his first World Cup goal in the second half as Germany defeated <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a> with 2–1 victory in their second group stage match to resurrect their World Cup hopes.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> He also provided an assist to <a href="/wiki/Toni_Kroos" title="Toni Kroos">Toni Kroos</a>'s late winning goal in that match and was named <a href="/wiki/Player_of_the_match" title="Player of the match">Man of the Match</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> However, his side were knocked out from the tournament after losing 2–0 to <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_football_team" title="South Korea national football team">South Korea</a> in their last group stage match on 27 June.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Reus is renowned for his versatility, speed, agility, technical skills, intelligence, and shooting ability;<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-best_wingers_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-best_wingers-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-talent_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-talent-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> however he is also known for his proneness to injury.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rocket_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rocket-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Franz Beckenbauer</a> spoke about Reus, along with <a href="/wiki/Mario_G%C3%B6tze" title="Mario Götze">Mario Götze</a>, saying, "...as a classic duo there is nobody better than the prolific Reus and Götze."<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Reus was voted the <a href="/wiki/Footballer_of_the_Year_(Germany)" title="Footballer of the Year (Germany)">Footballer of the Year (Germany)</a> in 2012 and was named in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="UEFA Team of the Year">UEFA Team of the Year</a> in 2013. In 2013, he was ranked as the fourth best footballer in Europe by <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Although he is highly regarded for his attacking movement, powerful finishing with either foot in open play, timing, and eye for goal, as well as his accuracy from <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct free kick">set pieces</a>, Reus is also a hard-working player and a precise passer, who possesses good vision, which enables him to create chances and provide assists to teammates, in addition to scoring goals himself.<sup id="cite_ref-talent_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-talent-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rocket_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rocket-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bundesliga&#39;s_best_attacking_midfielder_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundesliga&#39;s_best_attacking_midfielder-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McKennie_vs._Reus_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKennie_vs._Reus-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-solution_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solution-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> As such, Reus is a versatile forward, who is capable of playing in several offensive positions, and has been deployed as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Second_striker" title="Forward (association football)">second striker</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-evolution_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evolution-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> in a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Centre-forward" title="Forward (association football)">central role</a> as an out-and-out <a href="/wiki/Striker_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Striker (association football)">striker</a> (although this is not his favoured position),<sup id="cite_ref-solution_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solution-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-striker_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-striker-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">winger</a> on either flank (although he favours the left side, as it allows him to cut inside onto his stronger right foot),<sup id="cite_ref-best_wingers_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-best_wingers-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-evolution_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evolution-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-striker_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-striker-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and also in a central <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfield</a> role as a number 10.<sup id="cite_ref-Bundesliga&#39;s_best_attacking_midfielder_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundesliga&#39;s_best_attacking_midfielder-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McKennie_vs._Reus_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKennie_vs._Reus-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Reus is named after the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> legend, <a href="/wiki/Marco_van_Basten" title="Marco van Basten">Marco van Basten</a>. According to Reus, his parents were originally going to name him 'Dennis' but thanks to Van Basten's famous volley goal against <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_national_football_team" title="Soviet Union national football team">Soviet Union</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988_Final" title="UEFA Euro 1988 Final">final</a> of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">Euro 1988</a> they decided to name him Marco.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reus dated Carolin Bohs in 2009. They broke up in 2013 but remain close friends. Reus started dating German model Scarlett Gartmann in December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Together they had their first child in March 2019<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> and got married later the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reus has said that, if he was not a professional football player, he would be a pilot.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reus was the cover athlete of <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_17" title="FIFA 17">FIFA 17</a></i>, after being voted in by a fans' poll organized by <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2020, Reus and his wife, Scarlett, donated €500,000 to people and smaller businesses in need in his hometown of <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_coronavirus_pandemic" class="mw-redirect" title="2019–20 coronavirus pandemic">2019–20 coronavirus pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Reus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Legal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 2014, Reus was fined €540,000 for driving without a valid licence, which constitutes a felony in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The fine was based on his then monthly salary of €180,000.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> He had been driving for years with a fake Dutch licence,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> a felony in its own right,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> and has been issued with speeding tickets on at least five occasions since 2011 without authorities knowing that he was not legally licensed. The felony charges for using a counterfeit licence were later dropped causing some controversy and raising questions from politicians whether his celebrity status had been a reason for a milder sentence.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> When convicted, Reus said, "The reasons I did it are something I cannot really understand."<sup id="cite_ref-driving_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-driving-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Prior to his conviction, he had appeared in commercials for cars and petrol.<sup id="cite_ref-driving_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-driving-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> In August 2016, Reus confirmed that he now has a driver's licence.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
